de la char sor le neis	From a chariot pulled by two horses
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	 At no time do orifices of various sizes appear, from which some resemble many stings like scorpions; and if there are such, with an inflamed red hue, and softened to the bone-colored hue.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	 In that case of these joints which are exposed and not enclosed, it is necessary for you to make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; work on its nostrils, and pour the oncinate into those joints, and bend the fingers; then bind what you can grasp at the subtle agut of a thread, until you know that such a joint is completely ossified.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If any part remains that cannot be covered, apply all subtle and light rubs until nothing is left; if there is swelling or an abscess appears, treat as needed; and if malignant abscesses occur, quickly cauterize so the area becomes sterile and bone fragments are removed, then pour water, egg whites, or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	 If it does not work and moisture reaches the palate, know that it is sane; if moisture does not penetrate as it should, know that there is a joint in the bone above, from which strains do not come to tear: then it must be that you tie a thread of flax a bit thicker, and have it sewn on by us with space between each one; place the child's head through the knot as best they can, and stretch gently until it emerges from within the mouth; this method is often used for children in schools, and it is an easy task for those who know how to do it. Then hold the head that comes out of the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes out of the mouth with the other hand, and assess each as we are holding the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	 Do this as long as you know that the sores have corrupted their skin, then treat the son, drain the blood, and moisten the string with Egyptian salve, and put it back in place; do this for three days or more, until the ointment has dissolved all that is stuck to the flesh; then apply a plaster of any kind for as many days as needed until healed, and if dry medicines are required, use them; this is the way of the instrument used to purge the head, through which one distills oils and medicine into it.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor. de la char sor le neis	From a chariot pulled by two horses
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease known as "telul" arises at the top of one's neck, growing and becoming large enough to be visible; therefore it is necessary to make an incision from the start, and cut deeply, then apply heat or burning medicine; if not done before it becomes too large, observe carefully if it is hard, has a strange color, and poor sensation: do not use iron as it will worsen into incurable boils with each incision causing great harm to the patient; however, if the boil is from a soft area without discoloration and can be fully covered by an incision, reassure the patient, emptying them of fear, curing dryness and tightening.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the neck has been cut into
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	 Know that when continuous bleeding occurs in any of these cartilaginous structures, there is little benefit, even though it happens in some people.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Therefore, when this occurs in anyone, first examine if the wound is fresh with all its blood; then join the two lips into a seam and treat it until it heals; and if the lips are already separated on both sides, it must be scraped off all parts of their core as long as they heal, then unite the two lips into one seam, bind it, and powder with dragon's blood powder, and burn incense; and place over the powders a piece of alum stone from a strong or other alum stone until it exudes through itself, then treat with ointment until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of sewing is that you join the edges together using needles as described in stitching the abdomen, or with thread as I have shown to you previously.
des apostemes des levres	for abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the treatment of hardened abscesses resembling grains of pepper, both small and large; then it is necessary to return the lips, cut on each side with scissors, take them with forceps and place in each part; then fill the cavity after lancing a blister until the pus stops flowing; and then suture it easily, and treat the filled area of dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	For the erosion of gums.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Often there is erosion on the gums called "albulus" by the ancients; it is necessary to support them with pincers, cut at their root, and let blood or sap flow; then apply vitriol paste or other powders that constrict and dry out; and if the erosion returns after incision, and often does so, a second cauterization may be done: it will not return after cauterization again; these are the forms of treatments to heal.
des sordens	From soreness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	At no time are they gathered at the root of the teeth, within the mouth between the gums, which are ugly and sharp; nor do the teeth appear black or yellow with spots until corruption comes to the gums, making them foul-smelling; if it is necessary that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his cheeks be in your holy hand, and remove any teeth or splinters found, until there remains nothing; then do so with blackness and greenness, and yellowness and other discolorations, until they are healed; and if anything that was initially removed returns, it is good; if not, start again on the second and third day, until you have completely done so; know that teeth need various forms of treatments to be restored according to what the work shows, because those with which one cleans the root may differ from those found between the teeth; and these forms and others are to be prepared by you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when treating the tooth's pain that you delay extraction as much as possible, for it should not always be done; because it is a matter of high importance until there is no justification for pulling out.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	 Then when the patient's mouth is strained by sucking, one must be sure of the pain in his teeth.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	 Many times the pain distressed the patient, and he thought it was a toothache or gum disease, and made him pull out the bad tooth; but nevertheless the pain did not leave because of this, until the wrongful condition is gone, for we have already tried this with such patients. And when you are well sure about the tooth's looseness, it must be scraped around entirely strong to protect the gum from all sides; then move it with your fingers or pliers subtly at first and gradually, until it is properly aligned; then firmly secure the tooth. The head of the shoulder should be in its rightful place between his joints, ensuring it does not shift.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	 After extracting the tooth completely and breaking it, if it does not break off, take one of these substances and put them inside both parts gently, then move it as you did initially.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	 And if the tooth is pierced and infected, it must be filled with wadding where the roots are; gently extracting it with pliers so as not to break when removing; diligently work around the gums to dislodge the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	 And take good care that you do not break it, and leave a part behind, which will cause the patient greater pain from the severity of the roots.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	 And take care not to do as ignorant barbers who often break the root due to their haste and boldness without following what we have told you; but they bring about great disease from the roots that remain or from the broken root they cause, just as we have seen often; and when extracting a tooth, wash its socket with wine or olive oil and salt; and if bleeding occurs there frequently, apply powdered vitriol; and if this does not help, cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the sinews, to which one may move the bones first, are with long points and large knots, so they do not double when you pull on the thread; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be large members such that they do not bend while pulling, and made of well-crafted iron, and have teeth to hold when moved.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the bones

And it is also like grinding needles; and gently file the tooth bit by bit over several days so that it does not move too much; then smooth out at the end with a fine rasp, and if the root is too sharp and cuts the tongue, you must grind down the harshness until they are even, ensuring it does not cut the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth are loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	 When the tooth is loose through knocking or falling out, and the patient cannot press down on what they are biting without spitting out saliva, even after treating with medications that constrict, if such measures do not suffice; then you should use a thread of gold to restrain it, for silver threads turn green and rust over time while gold remains unaffected; the thread's thickness should be neither too large nor too small depending on the space between the teeth; and when straightening the teeth, take hold of the wire, loop it twice around each sound tooth, then place the heads among the teeth if there are one or more, continuing gently until you reach a healthy tooth on the other side; after that, resume covering up to where you started pulling.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	 Then grasp the head of the bone with pliers, and join them together, placing them between the healthy teeth, ensuring it does not catch the tongue; then leave it tight enough to remain in place, if it dislocates again, or if the wire breaks, restrain with another wire; it will stay this way throughout its life, resembling the shape of two normal teeth and their proper alignment as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And if the tooth falls out again, put it back in its place freshly as we have said; and do not involve anyone who is neither wise nor patient, and never attempt to form it into a shape like a boar'prise tusk, but fit it where there is an absence, and restrain it as previously stated, and it will serve for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	From heat, remove the ligament of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	 Never is this kind of joint that comes from beneath the tongue by nature to be made as such; or by accident during a sutured wound; and its workings are so that you treat the mouth of the sickly, with their head in place, lifting the tongue; then cut the nervous ligament wide enough for the tongue to move away from its resting position, and if there is stiffness or swelling, and it's due to a sutured wound, then apply linen and tie off again on that side; and be careful not to make an incision too deep near the artery below; and once you have done this, raise the red liquid and ice from the wound, then place a linen bandage under the tongue; every night soak the patient's mouth with something mild like warm water or cool water, ensebling they cannot swallow.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	 If blood flow occurs, put vitriol paste on the wound; and if it doesn't stop bleeding, then use the spot-cauterizing cautery which is good for this; then treat with another remedy until healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it to be colored or black or hardened, so that the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for this is cancer; and if it begins to ulcerate, and there is moisture, then drip on the hook, and fumigate with a delicate spatulaceous instrument, and release from all sides; and if at your treatment site, apply vitriol paste until healed, then return to the original treatment site as long as you treat everything thoroughly; then elevate cold water compresses and rest, and care for other remedeis till it is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	From abscesses of the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	 There are no times when 'godath', a term for swollen tonsils, occur in the throat; they are properly called "II amandres", and as we have described in the section on divisions, if they do not heal, take care: if it is an abscess of little sensitivity and soft color, do not touch with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	 And if they are red with the roots being large, do not touch them with iron, also for bleeding; but let it heal until it is scabbed over, and then you will separate them, as they may break on their own; and if they have a pale color and thin roots, prepare the instrument to cut, but first ensure that the abscess is resting and calm.

Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue against this instrument and see the abscess? Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, use a spatula with tongs like so:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And be sharp on one end and blunt on the other, and when you have opened one of the almonds, open the other in the same manner; after making the incision, gargle the patient with warm water, vinegar, and honey syrup if there is a discharge of blood occurring, then again gargle with diluted pomegranate rinds or myrtle leaves until it stops bleeding; then cure them until they are well, as none other sores than the two almonds may appear in the throat, so treat accordingly to remove both almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	 And I treated a woman with an abscess in her throat, which was of little size; and after carefully closing the entire throat, she could not breathe through the passage that was blocked, nor eat or drink, and would have died if she remained thus for one day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	 And the abscess had grown so large that it was through two openings made by the two nostrils.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	 So I quickly did it and inserted one needle, then the tool was turned forcefully, taking a large portion of bone; then I placed another in the other passage without touching the nerves, and opened the mouth and pressed the tongue; afterwards I inserted the needle into these boils, took part out, and only a small amount of blood came out; thus the woman's throat tube was cut, and she began to drink water then wine, and did not stop treating that boil for long periods; the boil would return, filling up the space I had emptied, until it became very large; then I deceived and cauterized inside her throat: so it stopped growing. Afterwards, I left these parts, and only God could do anything afterwards with her.
de l’uve	From the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	 When they are returned to the eye, and it is inflated and elongated, then it should be struck "perpendicularly"; and if it is devoid of thickness and round, then it should be struck "as an egg".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. de la sansue de la gorge	For the swelling of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	 Never is medicine without suction, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not help at all, then look down the patient's throat with sunlight, and press their tongue against the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	 And if you see suction, then treat it with all small hooks or delicate pincers like that.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	 And if it does not work, then take a waxed syringe and put it in the patient's throat, then frequently blow into the tube to clear the clog.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	 And if you give the patient water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	 Then take a full jar of cold water and work on the mouth, causing it to swell as if ingested, moving it often with their hand; and as soon as they feel suction, let it flow out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	 If it does not come out as we have said, then smolder the patient with tar pitch using the instrument I mentioned for smoke inhalation of the eye; do this many times, for it will take longer to heal.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	 The method of smoke inhalation is that you place the pot or where there are coal ashes, and cover it with a cloth perforated at its center, allowing the head of the instrument to pass through; then apply the smoke treatment, and have the patient put their cheek against the opening while closing their mouth so the smoke does not escape but fills the sinus. The sinuses will heal from there, and if it doesn't happen, continue with smoke treatments multiple times; during this time, let the patient experience thirst and consume unclean foods and drinks without water; eventually, they should sneeze out what needs to be removed by following this guidance.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	The form of the instrument through which you treat the throat is, when it can be seen, similar to curved tongs for inserting into the throat; and resembles a doctor's spoon, with a smooth surface so that anything taken cannot fall out; this is its shape.
li chapistres des apostemes	The form of an instrument like a scalpel and smooth it should not slip off.
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	 There are many kinds of abscesses, as our memory brings forth here from one and another in this book, and they differ by perforation and cutting; and there are two ways of dealing with it, one being the same and because of its moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	 And the second way is for bumps that lie on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	 For an abscess at the top is different from those at the base, and an abscess on the limb is different from those that arise in joints, and each has its judgment in practice.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	 And for abscesses that one should not pierce until they are fully formed, and those that require piercing when ripe, and do not die according to their completion, like an abscess near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	 When abscesses arise near the joints and are left until they ripen, through chance, the ligaments and nerves of the joint may become damaged, causing contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	 When an abscess is near the main limb, and if you delay perforation until it has ripened, it will harm the main limb; or if it's near the base, then pierce without waiting for full maturity; but only do so when an abscess is almost ripe, far from the base, to avoid premature rupture and allow drainage within.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And if it is meur l'aposteme que cil qui doumeit se li apemes sont la perforation and les mis li autres; or s et doree aseptement, et leas est pluses alés. Et quant il ne de tole du eunpercion ou as, telz apeme si tu l'apetes l'an, et doucues lontemps et meur esme en l’appetie se il les p.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	 In cases where they burst, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	 When an abscess is ripe for incision, you should allow the puncture to remain until digestion is complete, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	 For if you pierce it before this, the poison of his wound will run through his body and he is filled with much filth; and perhaps his lips harden and his deep punctures do so too.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	 And for any abscess that is pierced according to the size of their body, as needed by its member.

Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	 For the abscess may occasionally burst on its own when released from the swelling; in which case the patient might die unexpectedly, and you should not be held responsible.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Discharge this treatment carefully with great caution, and when you have pierced the abscess, let the wound bleed out, then examine if the wound of the abscess is small; and if it's a simple size, dress it with linen or old cotton bandages; and if it's large abscesses with much pus, it must be done that you insert a tent in each one so they come against each other; and if there are parts of the skin chewed around the abscess which have been cut into, it is necessary to fill them with old cotton or linen thread without moisture, until three days; then change it, and treat with ointment until it heals.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	 If blood flow occurs on your work site, treat with cold and soothing water, and wrap it in soft cloth, placing it upright many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If the blood flow continues, treat with care and remedies as mentioned in this book, and if it is winter or the wound or abscess site is very swollen, cover it with moistened tents and cloths soaked in wine and hot oil; if it's summer and the affected area is fleshy, cover it with moistened cloths soaked in water and oil or cold wine and oil, until after three days as we have said; then unbind the wound and drain and treat as necessary until healed.

Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke and told of the treatment for a throat condition; but I have never seen it in our land, and this is their written word.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with swollen throats, it is necessary that the incision of the throat called "epiglote" be made; and this cannot be helped because all the veins and the main artery causing great heat in an abscess are present therein, either in the mouth or in the throat or in two limbs.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is on the main artery's channel, it is necessary to expose the epiglute so as to avoid the destruction that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui. I hurried, stitched the wound, and treated her until it was healed; and nothing happened to the maiden except that she had a hoarse voice afterwards, and returned to normal; so from this, I say that in treating the epiglottis there is no cause for fear.
de la grosse gorge	In the case of a large swelling on the throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien. des pustules de la verge	From pustules of the penis

de la circoncision	On circumcision.
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not the dislocation of continuity like other wounds; however, when we perform this work by our own will, and properly for children, it is necessary that we make the best and easiest work for their health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not speak of circumcising their children, for they do not practice it in their laws, and we have only what we have gained through experience.

dou retenement de l’urine	Retention of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	 The retention of urine is due to stone obstruction, frozen blood, or bowel, or similar things that we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine does not pass and you see there is a blockage from a stone lodged at the urethral opening or neck of the bladeback, lean the patient on their knees; place their feet up on the back, stretch their abdomen towards the upper back, and restrain them as much as possible. Then constrains the bladder neck to expel the stone from above, causing urine flow; if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, then you must provide extraction with a tool called "catheter," which has this form: made of fine silver wire, about half the length of an ostrich feather's quill, and the outer diameter is about one palm long.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	 The method for the removal of urine is that you take a double strand of thread and tie it with a small piece of wool or cotton at each end; then place one head of the filament inside the syringe; cut off any excess wool or cotton, leaving enough to reach the top of the syringe, then grease the syringe with oil or butter and almond oil until it is evenly coated; have the sick person sit on a stool, and apply oil from an ointment made of oil, butter, and almond juice to their bladder and penis until they are moist, then gently insert the syringe into the penis up to its base near the root, then twist the syringe towards the belly; next fill the syringe with urine from the blad groove and let it flow out of the syringe as you feel the sick person's relief; this is not done according to this order for the reason that where the conduit goes may be twisted; then pull on the thread little by little until all wool has come off, extracting the urine; repeat filling and emptying the syringe until the bladder is completely emptied, providing relief to the sick person.
des maladies de la vessie	Of bladder diseases
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When scrapes or blood enters the bladder, or when gangrene is present, and you see it necessary to distill waters and medicines, do so with all the instrument called "claspdrue": this is its form.

de la piere	for stones
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have explained in the division how to remove stones and medicines together; and we mentioned the difference between a stone at its beginning as rain, and all signs, and which kind of stone one must operate on by cutting; and about the bladder, and about the penis; and I will now tell you plainly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which begins in the bladder occurs more often in children, and it is a sign that the water of the bladche leaps like spring water; and there are sandy deposits, and the male feels an urge to urinate, and does so many times before becoming inflamed; and from these jumps, the foundation becomes weakened; and for young children up until four years old, it is very painful in old age, moderate as those who are between youth and old age; and the treatment of those with larger stones is easier than that of those with smaller ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	 And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient with an enema, in order to expel all the filth that is within the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	 For it never causes any obstruction of stones.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	 Then take the patient by the feet and stand him up, moving them apart so that the stone descends to the front of the bladebag, and does not rise higher; then let him sit between your hands arranged, with his hands behind his thighs so that the bladder is fully inclined downward; then grasp and touch within; if you feel the stone in place, hasten now to cut above it.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	 And if it does not come out with the probe at once, grease your index finger with oil from the left hand, if the patient is young or middle-aged, and the middle finger if he is older; insert it into its foundation, grasp the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, squeeze near the neck of the bladebag; then press above your finger, and push out whatever remains wherever you see fit to cut.

Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere. A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors. Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	 And if it is very large, then one must wait for it to subside, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	 For there are two things that happen to the patient: they die or urine comes out again as the bladder cannot seal up; however, always make an effort with the drainage or debridement using forceps, until you have drained by pieces; and after complebing your work, dress the wound with incense, aloe, and dragon's blood, along with sutures, and put a cloth soaked in oil and wine or oil and rose water (or cold water) to cool down the abscess; then loosen the bandage on the patient's neck and leave it until three days have passed.

And when you loosen it, well anoint the wound with oil and water, then treat it with finished myrrh ointment and basilisk ointamoistened with clear water until healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	 When abscesses come into the wound and corrosions, and congealment of blood in the bladder, with urine being held due to this reason, known as passing without salt with the urine: therefore strike your thumb into the wound, extract that blood, for if it remains there, the bladder will be affected, and the kidney; then cleanse the wound of water and ease and swelling, and aid in all ways you know, until healed; and ensure that all bandages you apply are tied around both thighs, and assemble medicines at its place.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	 If the stone is small and it leads from the gland, and stuck in place, and urine cannot pass; treat as I say hereafter, that you may size it many times with a catheter.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	 I have already experienced this thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take an iron fork according to this shape, with three prongs bent at one end into a tine.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	 Then take a fil and wrap it around the staff underneath the stone, so that it cannot come back into the bladder; then gently insert the probe into the shaft until it reaches the stone; turn the probe slowly in your hand at the stone bit by bit, as long as you can pierce the other side of the stone; soon the urine will come out, then press your hand where any part remains within the shaft inside.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If it is soon broken and comes out with the urine, and the patient recovers; if you cannot do this due to any obstacle, then wrap a filament underneath the stone and another above, then make the shaft where the stone lies between two ligatures, then extract the stone forcefully, and loosen the ligatures, and cleanse the congealed blood in the wound; and heal it until it is sound.
de la piere des femmes	Of women with stones
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	Sometimes stones occur in women and if it happens once, the treatment is difficult for three reasons: firstly, because there may be a woman who is a virgin; secondly, one cannot find a skilled female who can undress at the baths, especially when she is chaste.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	 In the third manner it is that by chance you may not find a woman skilled in this art of hands; and the fourth manner is that if the stone from the woman is more embedded than the stone from the man, so one must make a deeper incision with great fear involved. And if necessary steps are required therein, then you should enlist an experienced midwife without cost, and if you do not find one, seek out a very skilled wise woman or a woman who knows part of the art, commanding her to perform what you require for stone extraction; and ensure that the woman is a virgin. Then it is necessary for her to position herself properly or kneel down, searching firmly for the stone; if she finds it, she must be constrained away from her privates and advised to hold them close or with the patient's hand on top of their belly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	 If it is protruding, then gradually move it from the beginning of the bladder to below, until it reaches the root of the thigh; then turn on the stone at the thigh's root against the flesh where it becomes visible, and feel for the stone in that area; do not rotate your thumb above or below the stone, and make the first small incision; then insert a probe into the opening. If you sense the stone so that you can extract it fully, recognize that there are many types of stones: they can be small or large, sharp or smooth, long or round, with veins.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	 If you know what to expect regarding its outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	 If the stone wins out, then apply saltpeter paste to its location and hold an hour until it is firmly fixed; then return to your work as long as the stone remains strong, and use the dressings I have told you about for home help in your endeavor during stone extraction; if the stone prevails again, and it's from a vein that has burst, apply powder at its location and wrap tightly with bandages and bindings, do not attempt this further, let the stone remain and do not manipulate it unless by chance the patient may die; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the fever of blood has subsided and strength returns to the patient, return to your work with stones as long as they are strong enough.
de hernie carnouse	Of hernia of fleshly growth
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	It is nothing but an assembly of moisture or white scab, which is under the surface of the skin that contains pus; and it's called "scab," and never properly in the tissue of the skin if one believes it to be another thing; and it's the leather part between the white scab we have mentioned, and nothing else occurs.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this carbuncle is due to weakness that affects the veins, and it spreads that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	 At no time does it come from the percussion on the joints, and this moisture appears in many colors: some are yellowish in decline, or without color, black, or watery white; these signs occur frequently to identify this assembly, as if it is similar to what we have described before, then it is a swelling resembling an egg's shape with short fingers and does not open the joints because it has moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	 If there is moisture in the wound itself, it forms an abscess with part of the fat, and because of this one believes it is another organ; and if the moisture is between the skin layers and the fascia, it feels quite well; therefore, when you want to determine the color of the moisture, try rubbing all around the involved area.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	After this examination, judge what lies within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And when we treat with iron, it is necessary that the patient be laid flat on their back for as long as possible and ensured body warmth; then they should lie on one side, placing plenty of linens under them, and command the attendant to stand opposite, extending the rod towards one of the two ribs behind where the shoulder meets the chest; then take a spatula-like instrument, carefully cut through the skin lengthwise up to the wrist, making an incision cleanly as much as you can manage, and puncture the flesh directly until reaching white fascia, draining all fluid out without touching the ribs but only the fascia; excise either in one piece or piecemeal carefully ensuring a neat cut, if not done properly, fluid will return; and if the fat bulges due to your work, have them resettle in their original position once you've completed the incision on the fascia; then suture together the two edges of the chest as with other wounds until healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the joint affected by another disease, it is necessary to tie off the vessels that are dilated, checking for blood loss; then cut the collarbone at its entire length and extract the joint as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	 If the bone is assembled in two parts together, know that these are two branches; join the other part as you did with the first equally, then let out blood, and apply linen soaked in rose oil to the wound; place another moistened linen in wine and oil, and put over both joints, and above doubled cloths, and lay a lie across all the ligaments according to this method.
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	 Then take two cloths and place chopped wool according to this design, sewing them together around the groin of the trousers; one end of the head goes up to the base until the back, and the other to the part by the elbow; the other two heads are placed on both arms, and all are secured in the loop of the braier; and this cautery medicine method should not be used as a foot-rule iron cutter, but take a delicate incision tool, prepare the skin over the joints, and soak it as we have instructed, such that the white matter containing blood is exposed; then use the cutter according to this design, pierce the vessels where knots are found, and scrape with this hot small cautery.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	 In all ways of dressing as you understand them, until you are certain; and ensure the fire does not touch the skin; and know that this work is more healing; and with careful attention to blood flow, and wards against swellings from incisions; and if anything contrary happens, such as abscesses or bleeding or other things, then treat what goes against it, according to what has been previously said.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	 And if the patient is fearful and does not want to wait for this procedure due to its horrifying nature, prepare as I tell you a perforation, just as I say; and ensure that when you are well informed by the meanings we have said that resuscitating water is laid, make the sick person sit on a chair raised up; then pierce the abscess in the area below all of the tissue widely spread out, and place the perforatur within long body cavities so they're fully open; and let there be wide openings for the water flow to be strong; then put cotton over it, bind it tightly, and allow the rest of the water to drain off, after which you treat until the wound is healed; and if a bandage doesn't let the water out through the opening in the wound, it must be that you insert a pen or an instrument used for treating bladder stones as mentioned above; then enlarge the wound slightly, know that the water returns, and gathers after six months or so, and when gathered again just as before, thus will pass through the sick person's days.
de l’aposteme des coions	If I; The old. Do not ca: f (st et les tous la:fle t ; they: c
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	 In this part of the treatise on fear and various conditions, it seems best to leave things as they are; and I will tell you about the procedure and appearances of an abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	But I say that many abscesses come from the body, especially in the knee joints, and this is due to numerous cases.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	 It is known by excessive bitterness and coldness that has spread to the joints or from percussion; and the color of the abscess corresponds with the body's natural color; there is no pain, but it is a severe abscess; and sometimes there are frightening and piercing abscesses with discolored hues, never originating from our arteries or vein inflammamoition.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	 When it is from our artery, it is known by the hot abscess's condition when you press with your thumbs; and it should not be touched at all.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	 The one with inflammation of veins is recognized by his tendency to express pain upon touching the joints, and he can well perform circumcision on this type, as well as others; and cut out the core of the scrotum, then extend it upward, and treat the white thread (vas deferens), and release the suspensory ligament from all parts of the scrotum.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	 If the scrotum is already swollen with these mentioned lumps (hydroceles), then it is necessary to treat the scrotum and remove them; and if there are stones in the vas deferens or within the blood vessels, one must release all that tissue completely, and roundly excise.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of a child is at or behind there, one must encompass it fully and extract the afterbirth as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your operations are complete, dress the wound with fine cloth soaked in rose oil and wine, then attend to other remedies until it is healed.

This is an abscess wrapped in a swelling resembling a burr, with the softening of tissues, and it causes the patient to move anxiously when approaching; and the cure for this disease is as fearful as that mentioned earlier, and nonethebout we will tell you the treatment according to what the ancients did.
