The quality of the stone is to seat the patient before you, and strain their neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, recognizing them by being black and having small black veins around them: thus grasp both, and if you do not recognize them, or are in doubt, pluck out the largest from each side, and do the same for the veins above and below, as they are of a similar kind.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	 of the stones underneath the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	 The stone removal from the veins underneath the tongue follows after cranial extraction and it's at the extension of the throat, and for illnesses of the eye, and mouth diseases; the quality of the extractor is that you must hold the patient with their head towards the sun, lift the tongue, and look below on each side a black vein: thus remove both, but do not go too far inward, as they are arteries underneath.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	 The veins of the arm which are commonly bled according to two methods: either by pinching with all fingers wide apart or with an olive-shaped tube, sharp as cutting knives, and called 'anesil'; and they are both wide and narrow depending on the width and lengthening of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the spermatic vein is highly reputed, and it is wide as you see.

Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz. And if you wish to know the location of its threads, it is necessary that you extract the arm and touch the area until you recognize the hairs; then signify the area with a marking, then bind the arm, and cut the flame as we have said; be careful not to hit the artery when you see the area swelling, for it is an artery: so avoid that.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez. If the wound is not closed and it bleeds, and there are no medicines present, tie off the artery if it is open, for the head of the vein retracts; and close the wound.

Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	 The vein's edge being milked helps it to draw blood from above the head and below the body because it is composed of both basilar and cephalic parts, as we have said; and it behooves the leech that it cleans its nerve beneath, and if too much pressure is applied, and finds the nerve, causing it to swell and become painful, and perhaps cannot heal; this nerve opens many times, and if not in any men due to subtlety, then you must cleanse it with an instrument called a lancet; avoid touching the nerve as much as possible.

The cephalic vein helps by drawing blood from the head and aids in healing; one should diligently squeezo the orbital or mirtin area, for it is the most beneficial of all veins as there are no nerves or arteries below it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien. Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The blisters of the legs heal openly because they attract blood from all over the body, and are effective against ancient pains of rain, of mares, and of the bladder; and they rejuvenate the two sophene areas, and the two ankles, and generally weaken the body after long use, bringing paralysis in various disposed conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The way to apply the blister is that you first place it on an empty area, and do so promptly, and set it hastily, and move evenly, and continue this action until you see the reddening and swelling of the location, and it appears with a slight flow of blood; then peel off, and reapply the blisters, and take care in observing the condition of the body, for there are those who have thick charred skin, and clear pores: if necessary, you must puncture only once, making wide and somewhat deep cuts, and drain gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, you must puncture twice: the first time to thin out the pathway of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	When the blood is very thick, one must strike a third time; and when we wish to draw out little blood at a time, it suffices for us only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	 And if we want a lot of blood, repeat often; and if the vein is superficial, pierce deeply, so that the core is quickly perforated, and it is suitable for those with thick and hard skin, as well as those who have been stretched out too much: oil the cords of the ventoscope with aperient and dissolving oil; if this is in place, violet or almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil; and if not, chervil, lily, or chamomile oil, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take oil of myrrh, or balsam, or aniseed oil, and other similar things.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	 If to those whom one treats with a tender and wide chafing ointment, it does not require the application of oil but must be washed after fomentation with rose water, or cold water, or blackthorn berry water, or gourd water, or porcelain water, or any similar substance.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	the li h; ce:
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	 Those with significant excesses should arise from old wine or blackthorn berry water, or anise or chamomile decoction, or similar substances; they must not use a vacuum before the bath nor during it, but one hour after the bath two hours later; and they must not sleep after fomentation, as they should bathe when necessary and if they have been bathed.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	 And keep watch over those who are pale and have colic, and whose stomach is too hot and inflamed; it is fitting that they consume cold things such as pomegranates, endives, lettuce, and similar items; mint puddings, and chestnut charcoal, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	 And those with a cold complexion should consume syrup of honey, and fragrant wine that is neither too old nor new, along with small portions of food; and the day they undertake it, they must drink more than eat; one must give some patients triaicle or musk before ventosation, or afterward, to comfort the main members; but only those who are hot should drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	 The suction cups that are placed without causing pain are those put on the liver, and joints, and gout, and on the belly and buttocks and thighs and hips, for that limb does not allow to be touched therein, and is done only to draw blood from one member to another as we do with nipples when they are not healed; to remove the viscosity present in the limb, as we place suction cups on the belly and buttocks to reduce the limb; and it removes pain, when there is swelling or a stone, then sometimes by its attractive power it may relieve the swelling, or displace the stone from its place; thus it acts when placed on the liver and joints when viscosity is retained, and these suction cups are provided empty to be squeezed as needed; and at times they are filled with herbs boiled in hot water.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of applying the bladder by fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	 And it has two pieces of half a palm in width, and around the hole a small opening as to thread a needle, also made of ivy or brass, so that it does not slip from the patient's hand when placed on the limb; and have within a rod transverse made of ivy or iron, for holding a vessel tightly, and they are large and small according to the diseases and condition of those who take them; because children's suction cups are different than old ones, and lighter than fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	 And thus this suction cup is to be placed upon the limb: take a wax candle or grease, and place it in the middle of the rod that lies across within the suction cup, ensuring that it does not burn the patient; then put it on the limb, with the previously mentioned hole positioned such that when desired, steam is produced, and the su cups are removed. Then take the grease as before, and begin anew often if necessary for your use.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	 In the cupping which is used for pleurisy, there is no penis or perineum, and it is shaped only when filled with water, and placed on the limb fully. And this is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	 Without cupping is used for limbs where one cannot place cups due to their size, such as lips and gums, or similar areas; and in cleaned wounds like donor or recipient sites, and other similar areas. The characteristic of the use is that when you find cups that are filled with clear gentle water, take them; put them on a cup of mild water until they become plump, without anything inside; then draw blood from the vein and cup together, rub the limb until it turns red, place the cups; and once they are full and tighten, if there is a location where one can place a cup, do so because this is of great value afterward.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	 If not, raise the limb with ease and then apply water generously, ensuring it is cold, and wrap in a linen cloth, keeping it on until the swelling subsides; if there are multiple swellings, place vitriol powder or ointments similar to these until they subside; now you may use half of peeled beans, leaving them until they become dry at the limb, which will now seal properly; and if more is needed, obtain additional poultices.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	 And if the swellings do not decrease, rub the limb with fresh blood or insert a needle until it pierces the swelling, then apply and as soon as they feel the blood, let them dry; when you see that they discharge, sprinkle some aloe powder and crushed sea salt, or ash, so they will harden now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These treatments are often necessary in the art of medicine, and are for repairing and replenishing.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	 Learn, O wise physician, that the madman seeks knowledge from this treatise, which has never been seen in any ancient books or read; and for this reason, its science is strange on our land, as I have found no good copies; though through the wisdom of ancient texts, to which I devoted myself so much that I acquired their knowledge, and by experimentation, and from the habits of my life, I have described herein what is contained in this chapter, and abbreviated at the end, showing clearly the forms of strangulations they performed, as done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we must say that the purpose of this book is to speak of words and chapters in which the wise man applies his understanding, staying true, so those who are experienced know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	 I say that when fractures or dislocaturations or twists or distortions occur in any part of the body, you must treat the patient with warmth on both sides if nothing is very weak such as infants or elderly; or if the heat is not too strong or excessively cold; and avoid fatty frosty foods like cold soups, poultry broth, do not drink wine, nor eat any greasy dishes, and do not overfill with meats that fill blood vessels until there are doubts of hot abscesses or discharge of matter in the limbs; then illness will return to its former state.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with meats that produce a healthy appetite and are like cooked wheat in fluidity, such as veal, lamb, beef, chicken broth, eggs, fresh fish, red wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	Because proper nutrition represents the muscles' quickness and soon after, the fracture is set right.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	 And know that broken bones of old and decrepit cannot be well repaired or joined according to their nature for limb support, nor those as tender as the bones of young children; but do not fret, reset using large strong pins which are sturdy and join the limb together, until it strengthens as if unbroken; and leave none of your work undone, and therefore it is necessary to nourish with hearty meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures occur in various ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	When a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	The feroit li cheint qui tu all the la manier: les ceste fait: le mone riguez de tesme ce. Et l'a estropidemane loron les pois congne et en telle, car il li prise est l’en tout li onques:
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	When there is a break with a wound, and a crack as a tiny split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	 Each way has its own device and instrument for restoration, according to what comes to mind in that place; and it is known there is bone fracture when the eye is twisted and opened widely due to pressure from gripping, and near squeezing of the hand; but if there is no twisting or feeling upon touch, and the patient does not feel much pain unless there is a breakage; however, it can well have twists, splits, or small fractures.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	However, do not just move the hand, but apply with medicine that comes here afterward and then gently stretch it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	 And know that the fracture which is in flight, and are the two parts disconnected, they must now be put back equally; as for abscesses if it comes to them; and if abscesses clear come, let him leave none until the abscess is soothed; then set it evenly with moves that you can do lightly and skillfully, and know that the restoration of it is easier than in those where pieces are involved; then strain, as it should be hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	 And if the bone is broken into pieces, if divided into two parts, whether it's hands or feet, or to your hand if it'amoebas', or small limbs, or at the cords, or a cord and your hand; put back the member according to its natural shape so that when the separated pieces of the broken limb are devoid, align them with all means in their places as moves you can do, and ensure by your craft there is no injury nor pain to the patient; and well-join the two ends of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And he feels well in the hand if it seems to you that it is not moving well: dress him neatly and do not restrain or press as those who cause abscesses to come out quickly and contractions of the limb, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	 And when the limb is fixed in place, properly instruct the patient so they do not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, nor turning, or otherwise; and ensure that the limb is secure enough so it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	 For when it feels no pain, then it is not yet fully healed, and you must place it in a suitable position so that it feels no pain; and ensure it is placed correctly, preventing any twisting as it recovers; the quality of the injured limb depends on what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	It has been said that the broken bones are of various sizes and shapes.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	 For there are small limbs such as arms and legs: they should be wrapped in soft linen cloth; for larger ones like thighs and legs: they should be wrapped with a wide sturdy bandage, so that the large bandage encircles the entire limb equally without any slack; then place light padding around it three or four turns depending on the size of the limb, and hold fast only at the top of the bandage, then move to above the fracture and tighten less, with the fracture moving slightly away from you; and loosen the bandage little by little until you grasp a large part of the healthy portion, then take another bandamenent, and wrap directly over the injured area; then return to the section below the fracture, and secure it moderately, neither too tight nor too loose as we have said in the first instruction above; then place evenly spaced padding between the bandages of linen or cloth until they are all equal, then apply a wide bend on top, and then put well-made supports underneath, unless there is an abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	 If there is swelling or an abscess, apply a cooling ointment to the abscess and remove the swelling, leaving it this way for several days; then bind with strips of cloth slightly wider than a large quill, or wood used for making grooves, or palm leaves, in this manner.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	 However, it is necessary that the strap applied to the fracture be slightly wider and longer than the others; its length should correspond to the size of the limb, either small or large. Then bind with strips in the same way as you did for the first fracture, then over a string promptly, just like on the initial fracture; tighter it becomes, gradually less so. It is necessary that the thread be moderate, not too thick nor too thin, and made of flax linen; because if the threads are too thick, as I have seen in the works of peasleteers who make ropes from flax fibers, this is a great mistake, for the splint cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it should not have less than two finger widths between each stake.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is pained by the edges of the stitches after being tightened too much in healthy places, they should place lint or ragged cloth under them to prevent chafing.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the bone is broken, I will tell you the treatment for this hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it does not suffice to extract all splinters from injured limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	 When the limbs are large, it is not necessary to always use splints unless after V days or VII, or more depending on the likelihood of an abscess forming; and here is how ancient masters would restore breaks, dislocations, and torsions: take flour that clings to mill walls, mix with abundant egg, and create this concoction, not too clear nor too thick, using it as a common method for the splint restores fractures in various positions, especially among women and small children, for it is neither too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of an emplaste to restore fractures and dislocations and torsions: take abareis and ladani and enule and asafetida and gum arabic and mugat, each X; myrrh and aloes, each V; alechil VI; and make powder, and the honey with egg yolk. If the patient's constitution is warm, use this emplaste because it has a good composition, and quickly restores broken bones, benefiting many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	 Another splint method for torsion: take myrtle and wormwood, nine days; cinnamon and aloes, nineteeen days; ginger six days; cardamom ten days, crush well, and pound with water or abundant egg white, then apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	 Another method of resetting dislocated joints and realigning bones from their proper positions provides relief for sudden pain, and if fractured, take new linen, and the meal mixed with ease and oil cooked, and place it on the site.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	 These poultices do not restore but are beneficial in cooling abscesses and properly alleviating pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of bandaging to restore broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earthy parsley leaves, grind them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	 Another method of resetting to restore the broken bone and to soothe the remaining abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	 Take roots of valerian, chamomile, violet flowers, wheat flour from each part; and grind, then mix with wine, and if the limb is swollen, apply the mixture with wet coriander water or just water, and do so.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	 Another way of draining more than the first, when an abscess is hard to heal on the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	 Take roots of vetch, and seed of flax, balm, mallow, melilotus, and marigold, all in equal parts; grind them up and mix with saltwater or fresh water, or wine, according to the warmth of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras states in his book that one should not place anything other than wax and oil on a broken limb for restoration, and it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that on must place dry and slightly warm things, such as myrrh, balm, frankincense, and similar substances, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of incision for injury and pain: take mugwort and horsehair clippings, or bird feathers, and wormwood, all equal amounts, and grind them, then make an ointment with the powdered mixture.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	 Then slightly move it again, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain or has lost bone alignment; if they do suffer from discomfort at the joint, swelling, restlessness, or itching, act quickly and reset the limb, then drain immediately; apply a light dressing, use a wet sponge in water, and soak the area until the itch subsides and pain is relieved, let it rest for an hour, then wrap with dry, moistened linen or oil-soaked wool on top of a cotton ball; allow the inflammation of the limb to subside, alleviate the pain, then resume gentle resetting and slightly more draining, but do not force it as before. Continue until healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see pus and redness and pain and swelling of the whole bone, and you need opiate and bandaging, then reset it as before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	 If nothing of what we have said occurs in the limb, do not dislocate it for more than three days or four or five or seven; and never leave it unattended for twenty days, as is often seen, until the fracture heals, and approaches the proper alignment of the joint above; then you should hold it even tighter than before, and strengthen its flesh, as I have said earlier; and if you see that it becomes dry more than necessary, know that no movement will come about; so provide this with warm water each time you dislocate it, every day, and loosen the bandage occasionally. In this way, movements are prevented in the limb, and quickly address what foolish healers do, which return the limb out of place: it is a bad practice, and I see nothing else but laziness and working improperly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various ways of fractures
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	 Many ways of breaks are, and various forms, and the causes are distinguished. For there are breaks that are caused by spear percussion, wherein the neck bone separates all the way up to the sacral region which is below the spine; and for this reason, this type of fracture is called "hatchure.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Where the sword cuts through the bone from above without being pierced, this manner of fracture is called "absolute"; and there are wounds from these two large or small fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is an embedded blow, crack, or stone in the bone, or a fall on a stone, or other similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is an open wound that reaches up to the skin just below or above the bone, where it lies on top of the bone, and this wound is large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	 And if there is a wound that has been sutured back into the bone as delicate as hair follicles, and it is a small fissure, hence this break is called "capillary."; and if the wound is made by being pierced with a stone, or falling, or similar causes, and allows entry of a piece of bone, and the space above the cut is as narrow as when locksmiths strike on their anvils, so within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	 And this occurs more in those whose bones at the head are moist, as in children's heads; and it happens in all kinds of breaks where small pieces are dislocated similarly; and I will speak about them specifically.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all methods of fractures through traction upon them, and examination with touches, and by the corruptible cartilage that is thereon.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known when the bone has been discovered and rubbed thoroughly upon it, resulting in a clear break.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	The cure the on the vint la pere maude, and discomfitur, douleur l'apostrement de les tement, et is not fie, and of les semblue.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an uncertain sign of hope, yet expect healing, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the pain first comes to you, and it is in winter, one should remove the bone on the fourteenth day at the time which you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is summer, hasten to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the tissue around the bone is not spoiled, and come the accidents we have mentioned.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	 And if the bone break reaches just to the cloth covering the brain, you must split it thus: and take the head from where the patient is injured, exposing the bone in all ways possible; and as smooth as the wound's surface allows, if blood flow occurs during the exposure of the bone or abscesses appear, seek help as needed, ensuring that you fill the space with linen soaked in rose oil; then let the wound rest until the swellings are calmed and bleeding is controlled; afterward, start removing tissue around the bone, which should be done according to these treatment methods: one method involves cutting close to the narrow front part of the shape.
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	The second way is that you have various thrusts of different lengths, some narrow and others wide, with points, and made of iron rods; and in lighter work, do not strike the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, it must be that you pierce around it so as to make thrusts with taps, not too deeply lest they penetrate beyond the bone of the skull, and there should be a margin or circle above the point that does not allow the point to go past the bebone; you need several of these, enough for each section of the bone's thickness, so have taps for all tests; this is the form of the three ways of tapers:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the bone is to place a tap on the bone and then turn it until you know that the bone is pierced; then move the tap slightly elsewhere, doing this all around, then cut with incisors the space of the balled which is between the pricks, and do this more delicately than possible, lightly, as we have said, so long as you work on the bone to your hand or any one of the tools that you have like pincers. And be careful not to touch the brain or the sacrum.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	 When you have pierced the bone and cut, it is necessary to address the readiness that has been prolonged by the bone from all other instruments similar to a chisel; but it must be more diligent and subtle than the other chisel; and if there are no small bones or scales remaining, lightly treat the wound with bandages and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is what the Galenists say, which is sweeter; and you must boil it very strongly, as they instruct.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you expose part of the bone where the fracture opens up, and once you have exposed that part, place it under the top edge of this lens-shaped incisor, which has the following shape.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	 And do not cut too deeply, and the part is numb in both sides, so that the cutting tool is toward the bone; then strike with a small mallet underneath it to gently break the entire bone, while ensuring you take care of the membrane above; if it's near the bone, handle the bone gently, for we do not harm it too much, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	If the bone fracture does not pierce through to the skin and is neatly cut slightly above, resulting in small pieces, then you must address the roughness again, removing scales with a subtle razor of which you should have various quantities to treat each area as most suitable according to the work involved and the nature of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If there are many large razors needed, then after using finer ones as well, continue to do so until it is done properly.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair trimming and delicate fractures, it is necessary to treat them according to their direction; and this is something that cannot be reversed for those who have studied in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	 If the eye socket is exposed, it is necessary that you take a linen bandage according to the quantity of the wound, moisten with oil rose, and place it over the wound; then take another bandage folded into two or three layers, moisten with wine and oil rose, and place it above the first bandage; and do this gently so as not to burden the eye socket, then treat on top of it with a medicinal substance without stretching it more than needed to just cover the wound alone; leave it thus for one or two days until the swelling subsides, then remove it, and administer remedies like lily root decoction, wheat flour, incense powder, aristologist, and similar things; from these make a powder, apply to the wound, and add more medicines without mordanting; ensure that the wound is clean without leaving any ointment or residue of cloth, as when cloth gathers on the brain's veil, it will harden and press down, causing great harm.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take care that if anything unfortunate happens to the patient, as we have said, it is uncertain but without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if darkness does not come through the medicine applied on it, that its virtue is effective, then you must take a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and wine in cloth, and apply it to the wound; then treat according to suitable remedies until healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	It is said that the two parts above do not break if only one moves at a time, for they are bones; and the joint below is cartilaginous and does not break, but rather swells or twists before healing.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	 And if one of the two parts is broken, you must sew your thumb or finger hole, and place the break similarly to your index finger, and through the same pouch as before, until the thread returns to its natural form; do this gently, and ensure that the patient does not feel pain from your action.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the elbow and cannot bring the arm to its place, it is fitting that you set it level with a small branch.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	 And if the break is in two parts, do it similarly again, and strive to restore within the first day; if not possible, after the seventh or eighth day, when the swelling has calmed down, then sew with lin thread at the head of the hole if the break is on one side.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	When you bind another with a band on the other side, if there is a breakage present; and let the swellings be such that they fill the nostrils completely.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	 And some healers say you must boil the threads with butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	 It seems to me not entirely right, but it must be boiled in a mixture of egg yolk and flour powder; then let the thread dry until the bone is firm, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never should one place goose feathers in the nostrils instead of swelling treatment, and if there is a .i. piece of cloth near it, this causes dislocation, and blows the illness upon them; rather do what you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	When an abscess is found near the nose while you work on it, then apply a poultice or cotton wool soaked in rose oil, or use a small amount of diacron.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if no abscess comes forth, then apply the poultice promptly, made of barley flour and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk, followed by placing light gauze; and do not tie it too tightly. If the bone fracture is small and broken into tiny pieces, extract as appropriate fragments, then align the fissure, and treat any strange wounds such as cuts or burns, just like poultices and ointments suitable for this; if there are no injuries within the bones, cure with threads soaked in pus.
de la routure de la mandibule	For a dislocation of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is dislocated and there are no resulting wounds, and the fractures are minor only, it should be examined lightly for complications inside.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	by and s1
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	If the fracture of the jaw is dislocated into two parts, it must be managed by adjusting the extension until they are even.

de la forcele	Of great strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The fractures break several times in front of the shoulder, and the breakage is in three ways: where it is broken and separated into two, with fragments present, and easier to repair; or there is a breakage with an accompanying wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the treatments are when there is a breakage with an accompanying wound, so that you have two assistants; one who washes the shoulder affected by the fracture, and another extends the neck towards the area; then aligns the break to your shoulders correctly, such that there is no appearance or unevenness.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	When you need to extend further, place under the patient's shoulder a round stick of cloth or woolen material, and make it thick according to your necessity; then stretch and release the tension, hold the stick in your hand, placing equal breaks as required.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the top of the stick with ease because it comes out at the front, then it is necessary that the patient lies on their side, and places under the shoulder half an iron bar; place the assistants' shoulders against it, until the bone in the forearm is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then you reach for the break to your elbangs, and if it is still broken, so that you cut underneath; gently extract the pieces, and if the bone cannot join due to any splinting, apply with a copestone from one of the incisions you have made; but place this instrument under the forearm to prevent swelling.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	 And it appears like a spoon, and is not sharp; its width should be as much as necessary according to the size of the bone and strength of the work; have two heads, as you see, one wider and the other narrower, just as with the shape of the wound from when you set the bones; and when you are certain there is no heat from the abscess, measure the wound, and if it's small or doubtful hot, then dress the wound with cloths and bandages according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if there are multiple abscesses, apply an oil-soaked cloth and linen with wine, and place it on top.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	 The compression of the bone when it is without wounds and without cuts, you should place on the bprise the powdered dust of molten lead and ox fat, then put light plasters over that, also use a stick under the knee if necessary; then take a very large bandage one palm wide, then lay double cloths over the plaster, along with the lead paste; then take a thin rod three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that bandage so its head hangs evenly; place the rod on the fracture, turn the bandage from the knee, and away from both the healthy and unhealthamalide leg; connect each part separately, and when you see the ligature holds the fracture in position clearly, and that the rod does not move above the bone broken, restrain it every day; and if the straps loosen, re-tighten them. Lay the unhealthy patient on his back, and put a small pillow under the knee to elevate the joint while he sleeps; this will alleviate pressure from the fracture by supporting the shoulder, or you may tie their arm to the neck, ensuring they do not accidentally dislocate it until XX days have passed; then restart the powdered lead if needed, and retain and release it as such, until restored. It is usually fully healed in up to twenty-eight days, but less for some individuals.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the shoulder fracture
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	 Sometimes the shoulder is broken or dislocated and cannot be moved; it should not be forced except by touching. Arrange according to the fracture pattern, and set the joint in its natural form in all ways possible; then put on the place powder from ground oats with plenty of oil, and light gauze; then put a double layer over it; then place a wide and thin board slightly wider than the shoulder, so that you can clamp the arm at any point on the shoulder using linen thread cuts equally; and then strain all firmly, so that the board does not move from its place, and watch the joint each day; and every time it moves, strain again, and align the board if it is out of place, and have the patient lie down with his side up; and after a certain number of days or weeks (XX to XXV), when these numbers are completed, release the clamping, and be cautious, for it is not bone that sets easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	If a bone fragment is sticking out and not covered by skin, cleanse the area, and treat the bone, following what we have said in treating fractures of strong animals with pus-filled abscesses.

de la brisure des costes	Of rib fractures
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that the fracture of the ribs occurs mostly on their sides after the back and within the head, and they do not bend easily because they are gristly; and they feel well at the inquiry with fingers.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	 And healing is such that you set the fracture as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	 Then apply the splint, and secure with a strap if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is leaning towards the head, it causes great pain and swelling to the patient, just like pleurisy, because the bone has no flesh; they also have fever, vomiting, and a large amount of blood loss, which is a serious illness, and the ancients used significant remedies for it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And of those who say that it should be treated with meats that inflame the stomach to drive away the obstruction quickly.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not cause abscesses to appear in vain if they have not come yet.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it has come to pass, so he is whole.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that one places cups on the limb to draw out humors, and it seems reasonable; however, there is doubt that the cups may attract excesses to the limb due to its weak condition.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one should cover the limb with moistened linen soaked in hot oil and place tents between the ribs to evenly distribute the heat, then proceed with treatment of pleurisy, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 And if the patient feels great pain that they cannot bear from the unset bone, and there is doubt in them, then it must be decided to split near the fractured rib location, and an instrument should be used for protection; then one must cut the bone, gently pull apart, and then stitch the two edges of the wound if they are large, and treat with splints until healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	 If an abscess comes to pass, then place on it with cloths soaked in oily rose oil, and position over the affected area; and while curing the location of the abscess as required, keep it lying down along the side or where it should be, until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	From a fracture of the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never comes a break to the bone in the neck, and rarely does it bow; likewise to the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	 And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if it will heal or not, be cautious if you see their hands become softened and swollen and lifeless, unable to move or stretch out, and when you prick them with a needle, they feel nothing.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure. Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit. Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	 And if, after being sovened on its back and wanting to rise, it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	 Says that they are deadly: do not labor in their care.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not occur, it is a more manageable condition.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is to apply oil of rosemary or olive oil if there's an abscess, until it's soothed; then place it under a supportive and dry compressor, bind with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; they should not sleep on the part where they feel pain until healed.

And if any bone is dislocated, apply heat to the affected area; then set the bone, and stitch together the two edges of a large wound with a sealing stitch, until healed; and if the shoulder joint of the arm is fractured, also known as "shoulder blade," place your left hand's pouchet on it, holding it equal to your right hand at full strength; then apply an enhancer compressor and cooling cloth over it, if needed; then hold firmly, and if there are dislocated bones, correct them, and treat the wound until healed.

If the fracture is near the shoulder blade, it is proper to place a splint behind the elbow and another over the arm, below the fracture; similarly, if the fracture is toward the forearm, it must be placed with slight force without labor until the fracture is level with the area, and with the forearm; then adjust evenly as needed, unless abscesses occur.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if inflammamoins occur, do not reset it until after six days, and apply a cloth soaked in oil or ointment to ease the inflammation; then reset, and the way of resetting is that you place the plaster on the dislocation, then assemble the arm over the shoulder, and put your hand under the shoulder or near the breast; and wrap it, and hold firm at the joint above the shoulder, until the limb is straight if nothing hinders, unless the bone is not moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	If you suspect the bone is not moving, use splints, and place on the fracture a wider and stronger splint than the others, with two spaces between each splint, and let each splint be so large that it passes beyond the fracture three finger-widths from either side; then strain across the splints as I have said at the beginning of this chapter on treating fractures, applying greater pressure while gradually reducing.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	 And if you see the seat of abscesses and swelling from what we have said, in the hour when you restore the fractured limb, and doubt that an abscess is hot, leave it bound until the seventh day as we have said; then check every three days the binding, ensuring no inflammation or vein occurs at the location due to excessive stretching.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	 If approached as we have said.
